0x4094fb HELP
0x409500 Help generator                    Version  1.501
0x409538 V-Series Help System
0x40954d ITyping 'HELP' at the top level of the interpreter prints this message andNlists the commands for which help is available. Typing 'HELP' at a lower levelI(such as in the MEMORY diagnostic) prints out a description of the memoryJdiagnostic followed by a list of commands within the memory diagnostic forNwhich help is available, then the global commands for which help is available.
0x4096cb HTyping 'HELP <topic>' or 'HELP <topic> <sub>...<sub>' gives help for theLparticular topic, or subtopic. For example 'HELP MEMORY' will print out helpKinformation for the MEMORY command, and since MEMORY has commands below it,Nalso lists the commands below MEMORY for which help is available. 'HELP MEMORYHMODE' will print out help information for the subtopic MODE of the topic
0x409846 MEMORY. 
0x40985d Interpreter
0x409869 Interpreter
0x409875 KThe V-Series interpreter provides a set of commands with which the V-SeriesKsystem may be tested and used by an engineer. As well as providing commandsPwhich access individual elements of V-Series, a programming language is providedOwith variables with arithmetic operations, and programs (buffers) which may use.looping structures and conditional statements.
0x4099de LCommands are formed in tree structures, so for example the memory diagnosticMis entered using the MEMORY command (which may be shortened to MEM), and thenDthe MEMORY diagnostic commands become available. To enter the MEMORYKdiagnostic from the interpreter, the MEMORY command is typed. The user willHthen be prompted with the MEMORY diagnostic prompt, whereupon the MEMORYNdiagnostic commands may be typed. MEMORY diagnostic commands are mostly singleGletter commands like a basic machine code monitor. Thus for example the
0x409beb command 
0x409bf4   E $1234
0x409bfe will examine the contents of location $1234 ($ signifies a hexadecimal number)
0x409c4d and print out its value. If you do not want to enter the memory diagnostic,
0x409c99 but want to perform a single memory diagnostic command, the MEMORY command may
0x409ce8 be followed by the MEMORY diagnostic command, for example 
0x409d23   MEM E $1234
0x409d31 will print out the contents of location $1234 but will not enter the MEMORY
0x409d7d diagnostic permanently.
0x409daf Buffers
0x409db7 Buffers
0x409dbf NBuffers are the name given to a list of interpreter commands forming a commandMprocedure. A buffer has a name consisting of an alphabetic character followedKby zero or more alphanumeric characters, is created using the MAKE command,Kand may be run either by specifying the name of the buffer, or by using theIRUN command. A buffer may contain conditional statements (IF) and loopingNstatements (FOR-NEXT, REPEAT-UNTIL), may declare local variables (VAR) as wellKas accessing global variables, and is used to preform sequences of commandsNwhich may be required more than once. A buffer may call other buffers and also
0x40a029 call itsself recursively. 
0x40a044 GA buffer may be edited using the EDIT command. Certain commands are notKpermitted in buffers, such as HELP, MAKE and EDIT which require interaction
0x40a0d9 with the user. 
0x40a103 DELAY
0x40a109 DELAY                 Delay for a number of ticks
0x40a13c Format:    DELAY <nn>
0x40a152 MDelays the interpreter for nn ticks. A tick is equal to a field time which isN1/50th of a second for PAL systems, or 1/60th of a second for NTSC systems. IfHfor any reason field interrupts fail, a backup timer will keep the clock>ticking at a reduced rate of approximately 1/20th of a second 
0x40a293 REMOVE
0x40a29a REMOVE                Removes (deletes) all or part of a buffer
0x40a2db Format:    REMove <bb>
0x40a2f2            REMove <bb> n1 
0x40a30d            REMove <bb> n2 n3
0x40a32a IRemoves the buffer bb and frees the memory space allocated to the buffer.#Removes line n1 from the buffer bb.*Removes lines n2 to n3 from the buffer bb.
0x40a3df DOWNLOAD
0x40a3e8 DOWNLOAD     (DOWN)   Enables or disables external serial port
0x40a428 Format:    DOWNLOAD <ON|OFF>
0x40a445 KEnables or disables port A of the MC68681 serial chip for use as a downloadNport. When enabled, data sent to the external serial port is used as characterOinput and is designed to be used to load commands from a computer such as a VAXQinto V-Series. This gives access to a more powerful editor and filing system than
0x40a583 provided by V-Series.
0x40a5b3 EDIT
0x40a5b8 EDIT                  Edit a buffer
0x40a5dd Format:    EDIT <bb>
0x40a5f2 MEdits an existing buffer bb. (A new buffer is created with the MAKE command.)KWhen a user has asked to edit a buffer, the buffer will be presented to theNuser line by line, preceded by a prompt of the buffer name and line number. IfNthe line is not to be changed, simply type <Return>, and the next line will beGpresented. If the line is to be changed, the full keyboard line editingHcommands are available to change the line. When the end of the buffer isLreached, the edit is completed. Alternatively, the edit may be terminated at
0x40a809 any time by typing Control-Z. 
0x40a828 Lines may be appended to an existing buffer bb with the command MAKE <bb>.
0x40a88d EXIT
0x40a892 EXIT                  Exit from the current buffer
0x40a8c6 Format:    EXIT
0x40a8d6 HExits from the current buffer without obeying the remaining lines of the
0x40a920 buffer. 
0x40a943 FOR
0x40a947 FOR                   Basic looping statement
0x40a975  Format:    FOR <vv>=<ss> TO <ee>
0x40a997 FThe FOR statement provides the basic looping statement similar to thatNprovided by programming languages such as BASIC and PASCAL. The statement willFset the variable vv to the starting value for the loop ss, and step inNincrements of one until the end value ee is reached. For each value of vv, allJbuffered statements up to a NEXT statement will be obeyed. (Note: if ee is8smaller than ss, the step increment will be minus one). 
0x40ab48 ,This command can only by used from a buffer.
0x40ab91 IF
0x40ab94 IF                    Basic conditional statement
0x40abc6 !Format:    IF <cc> THEN <command>
0x40abe9 NThe IF statement provides the basic conditional statement. If the condition ccIis true, the command <command> is obeyed. <command> may be a command or a
0x40ac83 buffer of commands. 
0x40ac98 ,This command can only by used from a buffer.
0x40ace1 LIST
0x40ace6 LIST                  List the commands in a buffer

0x40ad30 JThe LIST command lists the commands if the buffer bb, preceded by the line

0x40adad MAKE

0x40aded Format:    MAKE <bb> [<nn>]
0x40ae09 HThe MAKE command creates the buffer bb if it does not already exist, andIprompts the user for input to the buffer with a prompt of the buffer nameJfollowed by the line number in the buffer. The user may thet type commandsJinto the buffer. Input is terminated by typing a blank line or Control-Z. 
0x40af33 NIf the buffer bb exists, the MAKE command adds new lines to the buffer. If theMnumber nn is missing, the user is prompted to add new lines to the end of theMbuffer; otherwise, the user is prompted to input lines to the buffer starting
0x40b01f at line number nn. 
0x40b04d NEXT
0x40b052 NEXT                  End of FOR-loop statement
0x40b083 Format:    NEXT
0x40b093 JTerminates a FOR statement. All statements between a FOR statement and itsKmatching NEXT statement are obeyed for each value of the FOR-loop variable.DThe loop condition is checked at the NEXT statement, and the loop isMterminated if the control variable is greater than the end value of the loop.6(Terminated on less than if step value is minus one.)

0x40b6dd RUN

0x40e19b DMAC
0x40e1a0 DMAC                  DMA controller diagnostics
0x40e1d1 KThe DMA controller diagnostics provide a set of function with which to testKthe functionality of an HD68450 4 channel DMA controller. The diagnostic is/capable of testing up to four DMA controllers. 
0x40e29a NAt startup, the diagnostic is configured to handle one DMAC at address $FE0000Kand the interrupt vectors used for the four channels are set to 96, 98, 100Gand 102, with error vectors at 97, 99, 101 and 103. These addresses andHvectors can be changed using the SETUP command, and also using the SETUPKcommand, new DMACs can be defined with the provision that the DMACs must be@defined in numeric order, and a maximum of 4 DMACs are allowed. 
0x40e454 LBefore a DMAC channel can be tested, it must be allocated using the ALLOCATEIcommand, and when testing is finished, it should be deallocated using theHDEALLOCATE command. Deallocation is important, because when a channel isKallocated, two data areas are created for use in testing the device, one ofA16K words and the other of 8K words, and these are disposed of on
0x40e5c3 deallocation. 
0x40e5d2 JDMAC channels are referred to in commands such as the SELECT command. The )format of a channel in such a command is:         [DMAC <n>] [CHannel] <m>Iso that the simplest form of reference to a channel is a single digit, in0which case DMAC zero is used with this channel. 
0x40e6f3 ALLOCATE
0x40e6fc ALLOCATE   (ALL)      Allocates a DMAC channel ready for testing.
0x40e73e -Format:     ALLOCATE [DMAC <n>] [CHannel] <m>
0x40e76d NThe allocate command prepares a DMAC channel for testing by allocating buffersKto the channel, setting up the device address from the default, or from theMdata specified in a SETUP command, and setting up the interrupt addresses forLthe normal and error interrupt vector for the channel, and finally resetting
0x40e8a4 the DMAC channel. 
0x40e8b7 PRemember that if a DMAC channel is tested on a running V-Series system that the Iaction of testing the DMAC channel will probably stop the V-Series system
0x40e953 running properly.

0x40f74a M 1   Set up an array in memory, then use the DMAC in memory to memory mode toN     transfer the data to another array in memory, then check the results. An N     error occurs if the transfer times out, or if the transfer completes but 4     the data in the destination array is incorrect.
0x40f86c M 2   Sets up a channel in linked array mode, transferring data from one arrayJ     in memory to another, continuously, until the STOP command is issued.
0x40f906 D 3   Allows the user to specify by three parameters, source address,J     destination address and transfer size (words), and uses the currentlyI     selected DMAC channel to transfer the specified number of bytes from
0x40f9e1      source to destiantion.

0x40fa1b DPB        (DPB)      Start Paintbox Main Software
0x40fa4f Format:     DPB
0x40fa5f OStarts a task which runs the V-Series Paintbox main software. The software runsJas a task so that the diagnostic interpreter is available during painting.
0x40fb15 SWITCHES
0x40fb1e SWITCHES  Switches on CPU card
0x40fb3d *The switches have the following functions:
0x40fb69 ,*) Front facing rotary switch (SW7): Booting
0x40fb97 .  0   : Enter monitor on startup and on crash.B  1-F : Load and boot file from disk, and restart on system crash.
0x40fc0a 1*) Horizontal rotary switch nearest DIL IC (SW14)
0x40fc3d M  1     : Enter Paintbox software on startup irrespective of position of SW7.
0x40fc8c   0,2-F : Nothing.
0x40fc9f 8*) Horizontal rotary switch nearest two resistors (SW15)
0x40fcd9 J   This switch is examined by bits, to give any combination of the options
0x40fd25    provided.
0x40fd33    Bit 1 : Download brush.
0x40fd4e    Bit 2 : Download font.
0x40fd68    Bit 3 : Download font as text brush if one doesn't exist.

0x4119a1 READ
0x4119a6 READ        (R)       Read data from the currently selected card
0x4119e7 AFormat:     READ [Loop] [Mask <value>] [<range>] [= <data range>]
0x411a2a HThe READ command reads data from a specified range of addresses from theNcurrently selected card, and optionally checks the data read. The command willNloop until flagged or until data error if LOOP is specified; otherwise data isMread from each location once, and if MASK is specified, the data read will be0masked with the mask value before being checked.
0x411b91 KThe range may be a single number, specifying to read data from that addressNonly, or may be two numbers separated by two dots, in which case all addressesKin the range will be read, or any combination of these. If the range is notMspecified, all addresses defined for the currently selected card will be read
0x411cc7 in turn.
0x411cd0 MThe data range is defined similarly to the address range. If no data range isNspecified, the data read will not be checked; otherwise, the data read will beKchecked, and the read command will terminate if the data is incorrect. If aKrange of data values is specified, the first word read is compared with theNfirst datum, the second word with the second datum, etc, wrapping round at the
0x411e55 end of the data ranges.
0x411e6d 3Example:   READ LOOP MASK $0F 0..3 8..11 = 0 0 2..5
0x411ebd WRITE
0x411ec3 WRITE       (W)       Writes data to the currently selected card
0x411f04 1Format:     WRITE [Loop] [<range>] = <data range>
0x411f37 GThe WRITE command writes data to a specified range of addresses for theGcurrently selected card. The command will loop until flagged if LOOP is;specified; otherwise data is written to each location once.
0x412004 JThe range may be a single number, specifying to write data to that addressNonly, or may be two numbers separated by two dots, in which case all addressesNin the range will be written, or any combination of these. If the range is notPspecified, all addresses defined for the currently selected card will be written
0x41213f in turn.
0x412148 IThe data range is defined similarly to the address range. The first valueLspecified is written to the first address specified, and the data are cycled%through for each destination address.

0x412321          or INITIALISE All
0x41233c NThe initialise command is used to initialise one or all cards within MAVIS. IfLa card name is specified, that card is initialised; if ALL is specified, allOcards are initialised, and if no card is specified, the currently selected cardOis initialised, or if no card is currently selected, all cards are initialised.

0x42012f PATTERN
0x420137 PATTERN    (PAT)   Draws a test pattern - useful for hardware testing cursor
0x420184  Format:   PATTERN <pattern_type>
0x4201a6 ODraws a test pattern that facilitates testing the cursor hardware.  There are 4Kpossible "colours" available from the cursor hardware - "transparent" = 0, O"cursor_colour" = 1, "shadow" = 2 and "grid_colour" = 3.  All four colours can Mbe written to both the grid and cursor stores.  The pattern written into the Ggrid store is as follows - the full screen is divided up into quarters Ohorizontally and vertically and "colours" are written into the quarters in the 
0x420379 following pattern.     0 0 0 0
0x420398                        0 1 1 1
0x4203b7                        0 1 2 2
0x4203d6                        0 1 2 3
0x4203f5 The pattern written into the cursor store is similar, except that the pattern 
0x420444 is repeated every quarter of a screen instead of every full screen.  The cursor
0x420494 store has priority over the grid store. 
0x4204be The <pattern_type> can be 
0x4204d9   HV = horizontally and vertically changing pattern
0x42050d   HO = horizontally only changing pattern
0x420537   VO = vertically only changing pattern

0x4219cd FILER       Filing system utilities and test routines
0x421a03 KThe filer control subsystem provides facilities for maintaining and testing
0x421a50 the disk filing system
0x421a75 filename
0x421a7e filename
0x421a87 EA filename is defined as an alphabetic character followed by up to 43J(currently) other characters from the set of A-Z, 0-9, and .!_% (lowercaseLcharacters being converted to uppercase). Note that not all files have names
0x421b85 fid          File IDentifier
0x421ba2 LA fid is a unique identifier for a file which will continue to identify thatKfile even when its name is changed or the disk which holds it is removed or?moved to a different drive. A fid may be expressed in two ways:+ #<drive number>.<file number>.<generation>
0x421ca8 or
0x421cab  $<hex volume number>.<file number>.generation
0x421cda A value for generation of 0 acts as a wildcard
0x421d28 path         Filing system path
0x421d48 MA path is a means of locating a particular file. The commonest form of a pathKis a file name optionally preceded by one or more directory names separatedLby a '/' character e.g. UPPERDIR/LOWERDIR/FILE. The specifies a path leadingMfrom the current DEFAULT (qv) directory to the subdirectory UPPERDIR, then toFits subdirectory LOWERDIR and finally to the file FILE. If the path isKprefixed by '\', the search will start from the local root dorectory on theNcache disk. If the path is prefixed by '~' then the search will start from theNALTERNATE (qv) directory. The character '\' in the middle of a path will causeMthe search to step up, to the directory above, rather than down. Instead of aMdirectory name, a LINK (qv) may be inserted at any point. Also a FID (qv) mayMbe substituted at any point, in which case the path jumps immediately to thisMfile. Since any preceding path is ignored when a FID is encountered, a FID isEnormally only used at the first (and frequently only) part of a path.

0x4242f3 HThe restore operation checks and, if necessary, repairs a disk which hasMbecome corrupted by some disaster (e.g. power fail during write). It performsGa complete check of the basic disk structure, and ensures that all file
0x4243d3 structures are self-consistant.
0x4243f3 LAfter a completed restore, the disk will always be fully self consistant. IfLthe disk was particularly badly corrupted, it may happen that some blocks ofKthe disk have become inaccessible (marked as in use but not forming part ofIany file). If this occurs (it should be rare), a second restore will free9them. No more than two restores should ever be necessary.

0x4256e3 RANK
0x4256e8 RANK     Changes picturenet ranking.
0x42570d MWhen several devices are connected to a shared SCSI bus using Picturenet, oneCof the devices must function as a Master device, which performs theKadministrative operations necessary for orderly running of the system. ThisGfunction is normally invisible, but entails a slight overhead which mayJoccasionally slow down the Master. It is therefore advisable that machinesKwhose response time is critical are not made master if less important (e.g..standby, or librarian) machines are available.
0x4258fa JEach machine is therefore allocate a rank (with separate ranks for the A -HLocal - and B - Public - buses). The highest ranking device takes on busKmastership. If a low ranking device has mastership and a higher ranking oneKappears, the lower will concede to the higher (but devices of equal rank doKnot displace each other). Conversely, if the current master disappears, the(next highest ranker takes up the burden.
0x425a9d Format:     RAnk
0x425aae   Lists current rankings
0x425ac7      RAnk A|B <ranking>
0x425adf   Sets new rank for specified bus

0x42685d Commands are :-
0x42686d 4: Activate modem. Don't go online.
0x426891 5: Activate modem. Go online.
0x4268af 6: Disactivate modem.
0x4268c5 7: Reset modem.
0x4268d5 8: Shutup modem.
0x4268e6 9: Restore machine to default non-modem operation.
0x426919 10: Set baud rate (param1) to be used for modem.
0x42694a 11: Initialize the modem nvr configuration if other commands fail due to
0x426993   no config.
0x4269a0 #Modem commands are not yet working.

0x4283f7           {LOng|SHOrt}

0x42898e      |BYTE|CONt|NODBA|FAST|SWAp
0x4289ae JOne or more of these flags may be appended to either IN or OUT commands toMmodify the command. Only the Timeout flag should normally be used - the otherJflags hava arcane meanings known only to the cognoscenti: if you dont knowGwhat the flag means, dont use it - you ewill probably crash the system.
0x428adb KScsi transfers are mostly used to disk and usually short. In order to avoidGsystem hangs transfers are timed out and aborted after a short period -Jtypically 3 seconds. Some operations, such as tape rewind and disk format,Nmay take longer than this; the timeout flag allows this timeout to be extended&in multiple of approximately a second.

0x42b29f DRIVE        (DRI)   Selects interface, drive number, cylinders and head
0x42b2e8 Format:    DRIve <A|B> {HEAds <head count> UNIt <smd address> TYPE <type_code>
0x42b337 LSets whether the A or B SMD interface is to be used for subsequent commands,Oand optionally sets the characteristics of the drive interface (which are left Lunchanged if not present). The characteriistics are the number of heads for Othe drive are the number of heads (which should be set to 0 for floppy disks), Othe SMD address of the drive, and a type code defining the track layout of the 
0x42b4c2 drive. The type codes are:
0x42b4dd     0: Normal disks with 20480 kbytes/track
0x42b509     1: "Eagle" type disks wilh 28000 kbytes/track
0x42b53b     2: Paintbox floppy disk, with a single track split onto the two heads
0x42b586 Default setting is
0x42b599     DRIVE B HEADS 1 UNIT 1 TYPE 2
0x42b5bb     DRIVE A HEADS 5 UNIT 0 TYPE 0
0x42b5dd i.e. a paintbox floppy, address 1 on port B and a CDC RSD, address 0, on port 
0x42b62c A, which is selected by deault

0x42e715 NRESTORE
0x42e71e NRESTORE             Rebuild picture number tables
0x42e751 .Format:    NRESTore LOCAL|SUB|<#drive|$volume>
0x42e782 * USE WITH CARE *
0x42e794 Will rebuild picture and stack number table from picture numbers held in the
0x42e7e1 picture/stack headers.
0x42e7f9 It works like this;
0x42e80d 1) delete all user files, picture number tables, stack number tables
0x42e852 2) Create some new files for user DEFAULT, on the fixed disk with lowest
0x42e89b    scsi address (or the specified exch disk).
0x42e8c9 3) Scan through all pictures, cutouts & stencils and extract the number from
0x42e916    the header and set it. If the picture has two numbers stored for different
0x42e964    users, only one will be used and the other removed. If there is a clash of
0x42e9b2    numbers then the second picture doesnt get numbered (error message shown).
0x42ea00 PThe system MUST NOT be used during the restore, and MUST be restarted afterwards
0x42ea52 JSupports multiple fixed disks on either bus. As the system always uses theNdrive on either bus with the lowest SCSI id, the system wont delete any number
0x42eaed tables on other disks.

0x430533 LIBRARY
0x43053b LIBRARY              Index Library files commands
0x43056e Format:    LIBrary
0x430581 CMenu of commands for viewing and testing the Library files used forBdisk indexing.  An indexed disk contains 3 or 4 library files, for
0x430609 indexing items on that disk:
0x430627   MRF - Master Reference File
0x430645   FIF - Fid Index File
0x43065c   KIF - Keyword Index File
0x430677   AQF - Action Queue File (optional)
0x43069c HThe MRF is a keyed file all the files in the library are identified by a@unique key which constitutes the Picture Reference Number (PRN).
0x430727 EThe FIF is a file of all known PRNs indexed by their fid. This allows*the relevant PRN to be found for any file.
0x430799 PThe KIF is a file of PRNs indexed by the keywords in the title or other relevant
0x4307eb header fields of the file.
0x430806 FThe AQF file, where present, contains a queue of FIDs to be indexed orPdeindexed by a separate index queue task. This ensures that all write operationsKon the library files are performed by a single, local task. The file may be=present on its own to enable an unindexed disk to be indexed.

0x432233 HEAP
0x432238 HEAP          Print current state of heap
0x432262 CFormat:    HEap [n] [skip] [<Loop|Analyze|Occurrence|Both|Save|Dif|"          Check [addr]|Find size>]
0x4322ca NIf no number n is given, prints information on the space still available from 
0x43231a the heap. 
0x432325 If a number n is given (And not analyze), prints a complete listing of n 
0x43236f entries, starting  after <skip> (default 0) on the heap, free (+ ve sizes) or 
0x4323be in use (-ve sizes) with their addresses.
0x4323e7 Note that these addresses are the heap control block addresses, so they are
0x432433 8 bytes before the address that gets returned to new().
0x43246b If Loop, repeats every 2 seconds until flagged. 
0x43249c If analyze, counts how many occurrences there are of every size of heap entry 
0x4324eb in use. If n, it will only analyze n entries. If skip also, it will skip 
0x432535 entries before starting analysis. If Occurrence it will print the results in 
0x432583 occurrence order( default is size order). If Both, it will print the results 
0x4325d1 in both size and occurrence orders.
0x4325f5 Check will show walkback to indicate where the item at the given address was
0x432642 allocated.
0x43264d Find will list all items of the given size. Find and check (no address) will
0x43269a print walkback for each item found.
0x4326be Save will save the analysis just produced.
0x4326e9 Dif will compare the analysis just produced with the last one saved.
0x43272e save and Dif may be used together, in which case the dif is done first.
